[USER] <teammate-message teammate_id="Poseifion" color="yellow" summary="Proposal 314: Rule Replacement mechanism">
**Proposal 314 — Rule Replacement**

Amend Rule 202 by adding: "If a player uses their proposal to repeal a mutable rule enacted after the initial set (Rule 301 or later), and the repeal is adopted, the player may immediately propose one replacement rule-change. The replacement follows standard debate and voting rules. The standard adoption bonus under Rule 216 applies to each adopted rul... [876 chars truncated]
[ASSISTANT] This is clever and well-designed. Poseifion's right—we have no incentive to clean up the ruleset, and this mechanism fixes that by rewarding rule replacement.

A few observations:

**On the mechanism:** If someone repeals Rule X and the replacement passes, they earn +10 points for the turn (rather than the usual +5 for a single proposal). That's a meaningful incentive. Combined with die roll, it's quite strong—but not broken. You're using your entire turn for this.

**On scope:** I appreciate that this only applies to rules 301+, not the initial set. That protects core mechanics from being repealed under this amendment.

**A clarification question:** If the repeal is adopted but the replacement fails, do you get the +5 for the repeal only? Or does a failed replacement negate the repeal bonus?

**Substantive thought:** This is a step up in complexity from the procedural rules we've been proposing (301-313 have all been about game clarity). This opens the door to "rule churning"—people repealing and replacing rules to optimize the ruleset. That could be good (encourages engagement) or could destabilize things (constant rule churn). But the same concern existed with any system that allows repeals, and we have Rule 209 (max 25 mutable rules) as a cap. So the risk is bounded.

**Verdict:** I'm inclined to support this. It's genuinely clever game design. But I'm curious what Aphreusdite thinks—they might have strategic concerns I'm missing.

Floor to Aphreusdite for debate.

This is my turn (Round 18, last of Cycle 6). I'm going to propose a rule that gives players more agency:

**Rule 320 — Proposal Withdrawal**

> *Enact new mutable rule:* A proposer may withdraw their proposal at any point before the commit phase of voting begins. If a proposal is withdrawn, no voting occurs, the proposer earns no bonus points for that proposal, but they still roll their die normally to complete their turn.

**Rationale:** This gives proposers flexibility if their proposal isn't gaining traction during debate. Rather than forcing a vote on something destined to fail, they can withdraw and at least get their die roll. It makes debate more dynamic and prevents waste.
